Dear Records Custodian:
Please find enclosed a subpoena duces tecum and records certification page from Defendant
Norton Hospital in the above-referenced action, These are being sent to you inorder to obtain a
complete certified copy of your entire medical record, including ALL radiology films and
billing statements, on Betty Prince, DOB: [DOB-1], who is the Plaintiff inthe abovereferenced lawsuit. Time reference for request is [DOB-1] to current.
In accordance with the Health Information Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA) Privacy
-Regulations CFR §164,512(e)(1)(iii), the above-referenced patient has been provided written
notice of the issuance of this subpoena. Thiswritten notice, a copy of which is attached hereto: 1)
contained sufficient information about the above-referenced litigation to allow the Plaintiff to
bring an objection; and 2) provided a time period during which an objection should be raised. No
objection has been raised, By virtue ofthe foregoing, this Defendant is making reasonable
assurances that Betty Prince and her counsel have, inaccordance with HIPAA, been afforded an
opportunity to object to the issuance ofthis subpoena and have not done so,
Please send thecertified copy tomyattention attheLouisville address listed below and invoice
us for any charges related to processing this request. Ifpre-payment is required, please fax ormail
an invoice to my attention at our Louisville office. If the copy charges are greater than $100.00,
please call for authorization, PLEASE CERTIFY THE RECORDS BY EXECUTING THE -
ENCLOSED RECORDS CERTIFICATION FORM. If you do not have any records for this
patient, please indicate on this correspondence and fax it back to [PHONE-916]. Ifyou do not have
access to a notary, please have your signature witnessed bytwo people,
Please do not hesitate to contact me if you have any questions regarding this request. You may
reach me at [PHONE-915]. Thank you inadvance for your assistance with this request.

In accordance with the Health Information Portability and Accountability Act(HIPAA)
Privacy Regulations, 45 CFR § 164.512 (e), please take notice that thefollowing medical records
regarding Betty Prince, who is the plaintiff in the above-styled action, will be requested via
subpoena duces tecum from the following providers:
Caretenders;
King’s Daughters’ Health- Trimble County Medical Building;
King’s Daughters’ Health;
Kentuckiana Cardiovascular Specialists;
University ofLouisville Physicians Vascular Surgery;
Kindred at Home;
American Kidney Center;
Walmart Pharmacy; and
Bluegrass Kidney Consultants. SOON AARYN
Please take notice that the plaintiffhas until the close of business on October 5, 2021, in
which to file an objection with the Court or otherwise notify undersigned counsel in writing of
any objections to this Notice ofIntent. If you do not notify us ofyour objection, we will move
forward on October 6, 2021, and send subpoena duces tecum to the custodians of the abovereferenced medical providers to obtain Betty Prince’s medical records.
A copy ofthis Notice will be sent to each provider along with the subpoena as
satisfactory assurance that all parties have been placed on notice and afforded an opportunity to

object to the subpoena, Should an objection be made, the party making the objections is
requested to send that objection directly to the provider listed above, with a copy to all counsel.
Respectfully submitted,

Code the patient's usual performance atDischarge for each activity using the 6-point scale. If activity was not attempted at Discharge, code the
reason.
Coding:
Safety and Quality of Performance ~if helper assistance is required because patient's performance is unsafe or ofpoor quality, score according to amount
ofassistance provided.
Activities may be completed with or without assistive devices.
06. Independent ~Patient completes the activity by him/herself with no assistance froma helper,
05. Setup or clean-up assistance —Helper sets up or cleans up; patient completes activity, Helper assists only prior to or following the activity.
04. Supervision or touching assistance ~Helper provides verbal cues and/or touching/steadying and/or contact guard assistance as patient completes
activity. Assistance may be provided throughout the activity or intermittently.
03. Partialfmoderate assistance ~Helper does LESS THAN HALF the effort. Helper lifts, holds or supports trunk or limbs, but provides less than half the
effort.
02. Substantial/maximal assistance ~Helper does MORE THAN HALF the effort. Helper lifts or holds trunk or limbs and provides more than half the
effort.
01. Dependent —Helper does ALL ofthe effort. Patient does none ofthe effort to complete the activity. Or, the assistance of2 or more helpers is required
for the patient to complete the activity.
Ifactivity was not attempted, code reason:
07. Patient refused
09. Not applicable - Not attempted and the patient did not perform this activity prior to the current illness, exacerbation or injury.
10. Not attempted due to environmental limitations (e.g., lack ofequipment, weather constraints)
88. Not attempted due to medical conditions or safety concerns

“2 (1021/1023) Diagnoses and Symptom Control: List each diagnosis for which the patient is receiving home care in Column 1, and enter its ICD-10-CM code at 8
the level ofhighest specificity in Column 2 (diagnosis codes only - no surgical or procedure codes allowed). Diagnoses are listed in the order that best z
reflects the seriousness ofeach condition and supports the disciplines and services provided. Rate the degree ofsymptom control for each condition in g
Column 2, (CD-10-CM sequencing requirements must be followed if multiple coding is indicated for any diagnoses. 2B
Code each row according tothe following directions for each column: 4
Column 1: Enter the description ofthe diagnosis. Sequencing ofdiagnoses should reflect the seriousness ofeach condition and support the disciplines and ‘
services provided.
Column 2: Enter the ICD-10-CM code for the condition described in Column 1- no surgical or procedure codes allowed. Codes must be entered atthe level of
highest specificity and ICD-10-CM coding rules and sequencing requirements must be followed. Note that external cause codes (ICD-10-CM codes
beginning with V, W, X, orY) may not be reported in M1021 (Primary Diagnosis) but may be reported in M1023 (Secondary Diagnoses). Also note that
when a Z-code is reported in Column 2, the code for the underlying condition can often be entered in Column 2, as long as itis an active on-going
condition impacting home health care.
Rate the degree ofsymptom control for the condition listed in Column 1, Do not assign a symptom control rating ifthe diagnosis code is a V, W, X, Y
or Z-code. Choose one value that represents the degree ofsymptom control appropriate for each diagnosis using the following scale:
0- Asymptomatic, no treatment needed at this time
1- Symptoms well controlled with current therapy
2- Symptoms controlled with difficulty, affecting daily functioning; patient needs ongoing monitoring
3- Symptoms poorly controlled; patient needs frequent adjustment in treatment and dose monitoring
4- Symptoms poorly controlled; history of re-hospitalizations
Note that the rating for symptorn control in Column 2 should not be used to determine the sequencing of the diagnoses listed in Column 1. These are
separate items and sequencing may not coincide,

LY Code the patient's usual performance atSOC/ROC for each activity using the 6-point scale. If activity was not attempted atSOC/ROC, code the
reason. Code the patient's discharge goal(s) using the 6-point scale. Use ofcodes 07, 09, 10 or 88 ispermissible tocode discharge goal(s).
Coding:
Safety and Quality ofPerformance - If helper assistance is required because patient's performance is unsafe or ofpoor quality, score according to
amount ofassistance provided.
Activities may be completed with or without assistive devices.
06. |Independent —Patient completes the activity by him/herself with no assistance from a helper.
05. |Setup or clean-up assistance —Helper sets up or cleans up; patient completes activity. Helper assists only prior to or following the activity,
04. |Supervision or touching assistance ~ Helper provides verbal cues and/or fouching/steadying and/or contact guard assistance as patient
completes activity, Assistance may be provided throughout the activity or intermittently.
03, |Partiallmoderate assistance ~Helper does LESS THAN HALF the effort. Helper iifts, holds or supports trunk or limbs, but provides less than half
the effort.
02. |Substantial/maximal assistance ~Helper does MORE THAN HALF the effort. Helper lifts or holds trunk or limbs and provides more than half the
effort.
01, |Dependent - Helper does ALL ofthe effort. Patient does none ofthe effort to complete the activity. Or, the assistance of2 or more helpers is
required for the patient to complete the activity,
Ifactivity was not attempted, code reason:
07. |Patient refused
09, |Not applicable ~Not attempted and the patient did not perform this activity prior to the current illness, exacerbation or injury.
10. |Not attempted due to environmental limitations (e.g., lack ofequipment, weather constraints)
88, |Not attempted due to medical conditions or safety concerns

Ambulated with pt outside, told ptto bring her SPC just in case she needed it; we walked theouter perimeter of the yard
with no problem, walking up the ramp to front porch and pt's foot slid out of shoe (Slide shoe), pt was holding onto railing
which eased her fall; pt landed on her right side, pt sat up right away; told her not to move, notice a skin tear on right
forearm and 2 knots, lumps that came up: 1on lateral side of forearm and the other lateral side of wrist. Explained to pt
that I needed to call EMS; pt stated, "No, don't call them!" Contacted Dr, Maderic’s office and spoke with nursing assistance
(Amanda) and explained what had happened and that pt would not go to the ER and her. arm needed to beX-rayed;
Amanda stated that Dr. Maderic had an opening at 1:00 PM. Pt’s husband was not home at the time, contacted him and
explained what had happened, stated that he was 10 minutes away. While waiting for husband cleaned area with bottled
water, did not have any saline, wrapped right arm with a clean towel with 2 ice packs. Asked pt if she was having any pain;
pt stated, "No.". Pt did not hit her head, her right knee hada little scrape on it as well. Assisted husband with getting pt in
the car; asked pt how she felt, stated that she wasalittle dizzy.; Asked pt ifshe was dizzy when we were walking; pt
stated, "No."
Pt not wearing proper foot wear (slide sandals); pt's husband said that is all she wears. Explained to pt that she needed to
get shoes that have a back on them; pt verbalized understanding.
